  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_97e95a44-4c6e-4b8f-afa0-8571f70e8720'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer14512262346705215422"><b>A story about friendship, survival, and finding your voice.</b><br/><br/> Growing up, Mallory Dodge learned that the best way to survive was to say nothing. And even though it's been four years since her nightmare ended, she's beginning to worry that the fear that holds her back will last a lifetime. Now, after years of homeschooling, Mallory must face a new milestone—spending her senio</span>
  <span id="freeText14512262346705215422" style="display:none"><b>A story about friendship, survival, and finding your voice.</b><br /><br /> Growing up, Mallory Dodge learned that the best way to survive was to say nothing. And even though it's been four years since her nightmare ended, she's beginning to worry that the fear that holds her back will last a lifetime. Now, after years of homeschooling, Mallory must face a new milestone—spending her senior year at a public high school. But she never imagined she'd run into Rider Stark, the friend and protector she hasn't seen since childhood, on her very first day. <br /><br />It doesn't take long for Mallory to realize that the connection she shared with Rider never really faded. Yet soon it becomes apparent that she's not the only one grappling with lingering scars from the past. And as she watches Rider's life spiral out of control, Mallory must make a choice between staying silent and speaking out—for the people she loves, the life she wants and the truths that need to be heard.</span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1637051250?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1637051250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1215136485954066813">I was only three chapters in when I had this strong feeling that I would never forget this story.<br/><br/>And now that I finished it, I can confirm that this is one of the twenty most memorable love stories I have read.<br/><br/>It took me close to twelve hours to finish this book, but I don’t regret any minute I spent reading this emotional story. Maybe I could have read two novels in that amount of time, but <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26721568.The_Problem_with_Forever' title='The Problem with Forever by Jennifer L. Armentrout' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Problem with Forever</a> touched my heart so deeply I’m sure I’ll be rereading it again in a couple of ye</span>
  <span id="freeText1215136485954066813" style="display:none">I was only three chapters in when I had this strong feeling that I would never forget this story.<br /><br />And now that I finished it, I can confirm that this is one of the twenty most memorable love stories I have read.<br /><br />It took me close to twelve hours to finish this book, but I don’t regret any minute I spent reading this emotional story. Maybe I could have read two novels in that amount of time, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26721568.The_Problem_with_Forever" title="The Problem with Forever by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">The Problem with Forever</a> touched my heart so deeply I’m sure I’ll be rereading it again in a couple of years.<br /><br />It’s magnificent. The love story, although wonderful and dream-worthy, is not even the best thing about this book. <br /><br />Mallory is the star. Her characterization is outstanding and her character development admirable. The entire story is extremely well-written and convincing, but Mallory – also known as ''Mouse'' – will make any reader feel for her.<br /><br />I couldn’t stop thinking about her. It’s not even some type of girl crush. She’s the type of character so beautiful we're afraid to expose them to the world, because we don’t want them to be tainted. We want to conserve them as pure as they initially are. <br /><br />I didn’t want to stop reading this book, because I didn’t want to leave Mallory. She has so much to deal with I felt like by keeping on reading, I was somehow there for her. She actually unconsciously makes the readers feel like their presence alone can help her.<br /><br />It’s incredible. I rarely feel this way about characters. <br /><br />When we first start reading this book, we may think that there will be insta-love or insta-lust, but the author steers clear of those. Mallory and Rider have a connection because they grew up together and have been there for one another for a long period of time. But now, as they’re facing each other four years after being separated, they want to reconnect, to relearn everything about one another.<br /><br />It’s so sweet. Since it deals with long-term effects of child neglect and abuse, interested readers have to imagine there will be drama. And tears. And harrowing scenes. <br /><br />But in the end, when I turned the last page and I looked back at my reading time, I couldn't help but realize how fascinated by the story I was.<br /><br />It’s not perfect, but it’s perfectly imperfect.<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1215136485954066813" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16131762600466250317">Don't even bother trying to guard your heart as you start this book, because Jen is going to take sandpaper to that measly wall you've built, and you'll be laid bare. Raw. Vulnerable. Going back and forth between crying and swooning. <br/>Heartbreaking, heart wrenching, heart warming, heart everything.<br/>As a person who has suffered from anxiety since childhood, I can tell you that Mallory's reactions and the seemingly-small things that garner her anxieties, are RIGHT ON. Like, achingly realistic. I was</span>
  <span id="freeText16131762600466250317" style="display:none">Don't even bother trying to guard your heart as you start this book, because Jen is going to take sandpaper to that measly wall you've built, and you'll be laid bare. Raw. Vulnerable. Going back and forth between crying and swooning. <br />Heartbreaking, heart wrenching, heart warming, heart everything.<br />As a person who has suffered from anxiety since childhood, I can tell you that Mallory's reactions and the seemingly-small things that garner her anxieties, are RIGHT ON. Like, achingly realistic. I was breaking out in a sweat for her. I love it that Jen wrote about a real, broken girl, who shows us that strength can come in "mousy" packages. There are many kinds of strengths. We tend to value sassy, loud, vibrant strength over quiet strength, and all kinds of strengths deserve to be applauded. I could not have been happier watching Mallory's growth throughout her journey.<br />AND DON'T GET ME STARTED ON RIDER. <br />My heart...my heart!<br />Please read this book.<br />If you loved stories like Perfect Chemistry, Speak (no, this is not a rape story), and Pushing the Limits, then you will love The Problem With Forever.</span>

<div id="review_1203686167" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1203686167" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8429172-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595453256p2/8429172.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1203686167?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/8429172-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=too-much-of-an-asshole">too-much-of-an-asshole</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=jlarmentrout-books">jlarmentrout-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=ebooks-i-own">ebooks-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=awful-heroine">awful-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=ugh">ugh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8429172-laura?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1203686167" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7398009007975161208"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420429845ra/13223235.gif' width='500' height='245' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>DNF @ %75</b><br/><br/>Alright, this is a <i>no more, please, no more</i> kind of situation. <br/><br/>It was page 60 and I was already all about putting the book down for good but since I’m a loyal Jennifer L. Armentrout fan, I continued reading the story… and I regret that decision.<br/><br/>I’ve spent a few days deciding if I wanted to push myself and finish the book because I’m only like 100 pages left, but at this point I really don’t care. <br/><br/>I found myself skipping through the chapters and <b>maybe I’m the one who outgrew YA and I’m d</b></span>
  <span id="freeText7398009007975161208" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420429845ra/13223235.gif" width="500" height="245" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>DNF @ %75</b><br><br>Alright, this is a <i>no more, please, no more</i> kind of situation. <br><br>It was page 60 and I was already all about putting the book down for good but since I’m a loyal Jennifer L. Armentrout fan, I continued reading the story… and I regret that decision.<br><br>I’ve spent a few days deciding if I wanted to push myself and finish the book because I’m only like 100 pages left, but at this point I really don’t care. <br><br>I found myself skipping through the chapters and <b>maybe I’m the one who outgrew YA and I’m done with high school drama in any kind of degree</b> because our main lady here has been homeschooled until her senior year so we experience everything for the first time <i>again</i> and I’m not up to it anymore. I was very bored throughout the whole thing.<br><br>And when I wasn’t bored to tears, I was kinda turned off and slightly offended so go ahead and tell me if I’m wrong but even though there are idioms and accents and certain words change their meanings depending on the country, city and culture, is that enough to call it a <b>slightly different version of the language?</b><br><br>It’s like saying that because I’m Colombian, I speak <i> “Colombian”</i> and it’s different from someone speaking <i> “Mexican” or “Venezuelan”</i>. It does not make sense to me. In this particular case these people are Puerto Rican and this is the kind of stuff I had to read<br><blockquote>
  <b> “What...does no la mires mean?” I’d totally butchered the words like a typical white girl who couldn’t speak any form of Spanish would.<br>Her brows shot up again. “Why are you asking that?” […]<br>“It basically translates to don’t look at her.”<br>…….<br>[…]and the fact I was asking her to translate what she informed me that morning <u>sounded like Puerto Rican</u> had her little ears twitching.</b>
</blockquote><br><br>Eh, how do you translate “don’t look at her” and say that is from a specific country? <br><br>And not only that but I don’t know why people think latinx can’t finish a sentence without throwing a <i> mami, mamasita, cariño, bebé, bebita, etc</i> somewhere. It’s like the author is giving way too much emphasis on showing she has latinxs and doing it wrong. I don’t know a single person who says that <i>that much</i> and dear lady, don’t get me started the expressions. I’ve met a few Puerto Ricans and it’s kind of like common knowledge that some countries have certain words that are more used by their population so when I read words like <i>cabrones, puta (when what they wanted to say is bitch so they could’ve used perra instead), gandules (isn’t it guandules?)</i> and some like that… they’re not colloquially Puerto Rican so one might ask why the author didn’t get help or why she didn’t consult with real Puerto Ricans about the expressions they normally use because if you’re going to have characters from different cultures, the least you can do is learn about them to not make these mistakes.<br><br>Maybe I’m reading too much into it but I’m Latina so I care and I care about representation because when I was growing up most <s>all</s> the times I read or found a latinx character, they were usually drug dealers, low-lives and/or used to show how dangerous a certain neighborhood was because of them living there and that kinda was what happened here in this book and yeah, I understand the social problem and stigma that a lot of people have about kids growing up in foster houses and how little these kids are expected to be once they’re out of that system but it wasn’t delivered well. And I got to the point where I couldn’t care less about the characters and when one of them died <i>(what a shocking surprise… it was a latino)</i> I was like meh.<br><br>Overall, it was an overdramatic book.<br><br><b>Drama #1:</b> Mallory overcoming her fears after years of therapy all while dealing with her past.<br><br><b>Drama #2:</b> Mallory dealing with the feeling of being a replacement to her adoptive parents’ dead daughter and living under her shadow.<br><br><b>Drama #3:</b> Mallory re-connecting with her old best friend, savior, love of her life and all the memories that come with him.<br><br><b>Drama #4:</b> Rider’s girlfriend –and also the <i>mean girl</i>. Fuck me, girls can’t catch a break.<br><br><b>Drama #5:</b> Rider’s life. It’s messy and full of danger and death.<br><br><b>Drama #6:</b> Mallory’s adoptive parents disapproving her relationship with Rider and her not wanting to go to med school.<br><br><b>Drama #7:</b> Mallory’s best friend going blind.<br><br>There were so many things going on and I just didn’t care about most of them.<br><br>This book feels like the first draft being published by mistake. <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="7398009007975161208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1638341678" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1638341678" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1638341678?book_show_action=true">May 14, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638341678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6235382557325558835"><b> ::: FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED ::: </b><br/><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463420811i/19116777.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <em>"I know you might not believe it, but I'm going to keep you safe forever..."</em>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br/>This was a gorgeous high school romance that brought me right back to the intensity of falling in love for the first time. I've loved Jennifer Armentrout's writing ever since I read Wait For You back in 2013 and when I heard about this new book, I just couldn't resist diving it. I feel like there's something particularly special about childhood friends-to-lovers stories -- I lo</span>
  <span id="freeText6235382557325558835" style="display:none"><b> ::: FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED ::: </b><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463420811i/19116777.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <strong>
    <em>"I know you might not believe it, but I'm going to keep you safe forever..."</em>
  </strong>
</blockquote><br>This was a gorgeous high school romance that brought me right back to the intensity of falling in love for the first time. I've loved Jennifer Armentrout's writing ever since I read Wait For You back in 2013 and when I heard about this new book, I just couldn't resist diving it. I feel like there's something particularly special about childhood friends-to-lovers stories -- I love the shared history between the hero and heroine and I love all the emotions and deep feels that come when they're reunited after years apart. It had also been a while since I read a YA romance and I really enjoy those so, for so many reasons, this was a book I really wanted to read... And I loved it!!!<br><br>Let's start with a little of what the story is about first...<br><br>Mallory and Rider grew up in an abusive foster home without enough to eat and in constant fear of beatings. Even though Rider was only a few months older than Mallory, he took it upon himself to be her protector and to keep her as safe as he could in their volatile home. Until one day, after a particularly violent confrontation, he disappeared. Four years went by and she didn't see or hear from him again even though she never forgot him. Luckily in that time, her life improved. She was adopted into a loving home and given much support in her efforts to heal from her past.<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>I thought about the boy who made my chest hurt, the one who’d promised me forever. It had been years since I’d seem him or even heard him speak. Four years of trying to erase everything that had to do with that portion of my childhood, but I remembered him. I wondered about him.<br>How could I not? I always would.<br>He had been the sole reason I survived the house we’d grown up in.</em>
</blockquote><br><br>Years of homeschooling had helped her heal and given her the strength to decide to attend her senior year in a public school. Despite her conviction, this was no easy feat for her as even something as simple as talking publicly gave her extreme anxiety. But the last thing she expected on her first day was to see Rider Stark. The boy who'd protected her, who she hadn't seen in four years, right there in her class.<br><br>Their reunion was intensified by the relief of finding each other again after years of not knowing what had happened and complicated by their attraction to each other, but their situation was anything but simple and starting off as friends was best for them given everything that was going on. As she got to know Rider again though, she quickly learned that despite being well, he was also caught up with people that were slowly spiraling out of control. All those years ago, he'd saved her over and over again. And now it was time for her to return the favor.<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>"Be careful," I whispered...<br>Rider's grin faded from his handsome face. I moment passed before he spoke, "Always."</em>
</blockquote><br><br>It's been a while since I've read a real high school YA romance and I have to say I really loved it. All the emotions, thrills, and intensity of falling in love for the first time made my heart race as Rider and Mallory slowly began to acknowledge their feelings for each other. For the record, he does have a girlfriend in the beginning. This isn't really a love triangle and the girlfriend wasn't serious by any means but still, I know there are some of you who'd just want to know what to expect. Even though they start as just friends, it's quite obvious to the reader that Mallory is the girl he cares most about and nobody is going to stop him from spending time with her. See, he even says this...<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>"She understands that if I have to pick between you two, it's not going to be her."</em>
</blockquote><br><br>... and there's no cheating. He's quite upfront with his girlfriend about how much Mallory meant to him and that he was going to be spending lots of time with her. So even though it took the a while to sort out their dynamic and work out their relationship, you always knew that Mallory and Rider were meant to be.<br><br>Falling in love for the first time, especially when it's with the person who you know you'll want to be with forever, is always intense and for them, with their shared past, pain, and connection, the intensity of their emotional connection ran deep and they not only were falling for each other, but shared a deep bond of understanding.<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>"I never stopped thinking about you," he said in a low voice. "Not one day, Mallory."</em>
</blockquote><br><br>This story isn't just a romance though... Mallory's growth over the course of the book as she came out of her shell and gained the courage to truly be who she wanted to be sent a strong message about bring true to yourself, reaching for your dreams, and choosing what makes you happy for you -- not in an effort to please other people. It really drove home how your life wasn't defined by your circumstance, but by who you were and what you strove to be.<br><br>As I neared the end of the book, my heart raced with anticipation -- I swear it did not seem like there were enough pages to fully resolve the story but thankfully there were! Those pages really flew by and the ending was beautiful.<br><br>I'm so glad I read this book. I loved the writing, I swooned over the story, I cared for the characters, and I highly recommend this for anyone looking for a wonderful YA romance to fall in love with!<br><br><strong>Rating: 4.5 stars! Standalone YA romance.</strong><br> <br> 	 <strong><a href="http://amzn.to/1TDSDai" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Buy THE PROBLEM WITH FOREVER (Kindle)</a></strong> <br> 	 <a href="http://amzn.to/27pEVSo" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><strong>Buy THE PROBLEM WITH FOREVER (Hardcover)</strong></a> <br>__________________________<br><br><b> For more of my reviews, book news and updates:<br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Main blog: Aestas Book Blog</a><br>✦ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook Blog Page</a><br>✦ <a href="https://twitter.com/AestasBookBlog" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> <br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com/subscribe/" rel="nofollow noopener">Subscribe by email</a> <br><br><a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380306821i/688100._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> </b> </span>

  <i>‘forever was my heartbeat and it was the hope tomorrow held. forever was knowing moments of weakness didnt equate to an eternity of them. forever was knowing that i was strong.’</i>

  <span id="freeText3623501718424881837" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>‘forever was my heartbeat and it was the hope tomorrow held. forever was knowing moments of weakness didnt equate to an eternity of them. forever was knowing that i was strong.’</i>
</b><br /><br />this book is filled to the brim with life lessons but, if anything, this story is the epitome of what it means to love and be loved. and its that second part, how to accept love, that i think is the most important.<br /><br />the connection and history between mallory and rider is so, so special. there were multiple times whilst reading this that it felt like my heart was going to burst because it was filled with so much tender emotion. i absolutely adored how they supported and healed each other, proving to each other that they were both worthy of love. <br /><br />JLA has always been one of my fave authors, but her contemporary stories are where i think she excels. this is hands down one of my favourite YA contemporary romance stories of all time, without a doubt. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>5 stars</i></b></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1650212772" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1567161463400153843"><b>2.5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"I couldn't put my finger on the exact moment I'd become a different Mallory. Maybe because it wasn't just a moment but more of a combination of hundreds, even thousands of them. <br/><br/>[...]<br/><br/>And it was knowing that I could still be...still be afraid of everything, but not letting that fear stop me from living."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398696535ra/9451499.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I sighed as I stared at my laptop screen.<br/><br/><i>Do I really want to do this?</i> I thought, tousling my hair sexily because I am a bookworm and bookworms are secretly hot as fuck once they ditc</span>
  <span id="freeText1567161463400153843" style="display:none"><b>2.5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"I couldn't put my finger on the exact moment I'd become a different Mallory. Maybe because it wasn't just a moment but more of a combination of hundreds, even thousands of them. <br><br>[...]<br><br>And it was knowing that I could still be...still be afraid of everything, but not letting that fear stop me from living."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1398696535ra/9451499.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I sighed as I stared at my laptop screen.<br><br><i>Do I really want to do this?</i> I thought, tousling my hair sexily because I am a bookworm and bookworms are secretly hot as fuck once they ditch their glasses. <i>Do I really want to bash a book that, in all honesty, appeals to my values?</i><br><br><i>Yes! </i>a dark, fanged part of me shouted. A part of me I'd dubbed Cynical Natalie and seemed to grow with each negative review I wrote. Soon, she'd overwhelm me like Mr. Hyde and I'd be nothing more than a tiny corner of light in my own mind, screaming for help, as she posted gif after gif of Taylor Swift rolling her eyes.<br><br>I shivered. I don't want to be that girl. Mallory wasn't that bad. She was different from JLA's usual heroine: meek and shy. She had a mental speech impediment and she conquered it all by herself. And the rant on mansplaining and a little speech on why the First Amendment isn't a free pass for spewing crap was pretty nice. That's worth points. <br><br>I stared out the window. Pink tinged the sky in a very metaphorical way. <br><br>But I do feel like punching her. I sympathize with her, but I also want to punch her. <br><br>Hm, this is a conundrum.<br><br><i>What do you think?</i> I asked Cynical Natalie.<br><br><i>DEATH TO STAIRS!</i> she shrieked.<br><br><i>Well, that makes no sense.</i> Biting down on my lower lip, I read over the notes I'd made.<br><br>Shot game, huh? Like that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/732372672" rel="nofollow noopener">other JLA book I reviewed. </a><br><br>I flexed my fingers and began to type:<br><br>Take a shot whenever Rider's fucking grin and dimples are mentioned. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1401695844ra/9834081.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When he lowers his lashes.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471360118ra/20036259.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When his hotness is mentioned:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471360118ra/20036260.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When you see ellipses. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471360118ra/20036261.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When Mallory channels Ana Steele and says "Oh my" or "Oh my gosh."<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471360118ra/20036262.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When the writing tries to be fancy and philosophical, but makes no sense when you think about it:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"...the way he said Mouse was so different from how Paige hurled the nickname. It was soft and deep and infinite."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457055539ra/18314226.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Bonus points!</b><br><br>Ten shots when you realize Rider is simply Daemon Black/Cam/every JLA love interest in different clothes and with differently colored eyes and hair.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471360118ra/20036263.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Twenty shots when this line shows because I didn't pay for an E.L. James metaphor:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"The blush turned my face into a breathing strawberry."</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471360118ra/20036264.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Two hundred more for the pages that could've been shaved off.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471360118ra/20036265.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I realized I was grinning and my hands recoiled from the keyboard like a hot stove or a snotty tissue. What was I doing? I said I wouldn't bash this book! Yet here it was, my seething, ink-black hatred, oozing all over the screen.<br><br>Hurriedly, I pressed Crtl+A and prepared to delete the whole thing and start over. <br><br>My finger stalled above the button, quivering.<br><br>Then again, none of what I said was untruthful. I did <i>not</i> like The Problem of Forever. I shouldn't pretend like I did.<br><br>And I spent an hour on this when I should be doing real writing.<br><br>Sighing, I pressed "Save" and watched my bubbling, spitting mess of poisonous thoughts get turned into zeroes and ones and be forever immortalized on the Internet. I pulled up my blank Word document again and looked at it.<br><br><i>Eh, I'll do it later.</i><br><br>I clicked season 3 of <i>Breaking Bad</i>.<br><br>(I apologize for this review, guys. It's super weird.)<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="1567161463400153843" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1713306522" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1713306522" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1713306522?book_show_action=true">Jul 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1713306522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6602612006141341519">(UGH I'M SO MAD my review deleted before it could upload and it was a freakishly great review too.)<br/><br/>Excuse me but <b>THIS BOOK JUST BROKE MY HEART IN THE BEST POSSIBLE WAY.</b> I loved it, I so so loved it. It just had aaall the right things, like delicious food, tons of diversity, adorable tragic damaged cinnamon roll characters, and a bit of bleeding (ALL THE GOOD BOOKS HAVE A BIT O' BLOOD) and did I mention I'm <i>feeling</i> all the things??? BECAUSE I AM. This book definitely won me over omg.<br/><br/>Wow...just wo</span>
  <span id="freeText6602612006141341519" style="display:none">(UGH I'M SO MAD my review deleted before it could upload and it was a freakishly great review too.)<br /><br />Excuse me but <b>THIS BOOK JUST BROKE MY HEART IN THE BEST POSSIBLE WAY.</b> I loved it, I so so loved it. It just had aaall the right things, like delicious food, tons of diversity, adorable tragic damaged cinnamon roll characters, and a bit of bleeding (ALL THE GOOD BOOKS HAVE A BIT O' BLOOD) and did I mention I'm <i>feeling</i> all the things??? BECAUSE I AM. This book definitely won me over omg.<br /><br />Wow...just wow oh wow. I would totally give this <b>4.5-stars</b> if goodreads did half stars (curse you goodreads for not GIVING US HALF STAR OPTIONS)<br /><br /><b>Mallory was an amazingly complex and winning protagonist.</b> She's been horrible abused in a foster-care-home for most of her life, and only got adopted at 13 by really loving people. Then she was homeschooled and now, for some bizarre reason, she's going to highschool. Like, I love ya, Mallory, BUT HOMESCHOOLINGFTW. (#HomeschoolerGraduate ahem) <b>She also has a lot of trouble speaking.</b> It's partially social anxiety, but partially because of the abuse she received as a kid whenever she made a sound. She's been conditioned to silence, basically. MY HEART BLEEDS FOR HER. She feels stuck and she doesn't want to be this way and she TRIES SO HARD. <b>She's just relatable and awesome, basically.</b><br /><br /><b>And then there is the precious cupcake: Rider Stark.</b> He was Mallory's foster brother, but they haven't seen each other in like 4 or 5 years. And BOOM. He's at the same highschool. THEY HAVE SO MUCH CHEMISTRY AND HISTORY TOGETHER. Like, the feelings, not the school subjects. Because pfft, school, who has time for that anyway. <b>I absolutely loved Rider.</b> He has the slightly bad-boy-with-heart-of-gold thing going on WHICH I ADORE. &lt;3 He's very damaged emotionally, but kind of doesn't even notice it of himself? He's super artistic. SO ARTISTIC OMG. And he is just all around precious. I love the complexity of his relationship with Mallory and how they faaaaall for each other.<br /><br />[aggressively ships them]<br /><br /><b>I also loved all the diversity!</b> Mallory's adoptive parents are Latino (I think) and Rider is half Puerto Rican, and most of the secondary characters are POC too!<br /><br /><b>The writing is just absolutely delicious...and addictive!</b> THE STORY IS ADDICTIVE. I mean, it's not entirely original, but it was beautifully and poignantly done. It's 500-pages and I read it in one day?! SO THERE'S THAT.<br /><br /><b>I love love loved all the food too, omg.</b> And I had delicious quotes saved BEFORE THE FREAKING REVIEW DELETED ITSELF *sobbing* So just imagine me describing cheesy enchiladas and ice cream escapades and you've got the idea of how glorious this book is.<br /><br /><b>And I'm <i>so</i> intensely a fan of how complex all the characters were.</b> For me, characters are the #1 reason I adore a book. I JUST NEED THEM TO BE GREAT. They were here!! Even the secondary characters shone in just a few paragraphs. Love love love.<br /><br /><b>OTHER GLORIOUS THINGS:</b><br />• There are such beautiful quotes about being shy/quiet but still loving yourself for you who you are<br />• There is a bit of banter (not a ton, but it is good)<br />• THERE IS ART I LOVE ART<br />• The cover is so gorgeous, I think that needs mentioning<br />• The romance is ajfdksalfdj everything basically.<br />• Oh and .... at one point it kind of RIPPED OUT MY HEART AND STOMPED ON IT. So there's that.<br /><br /><br />...okay but there were a <i>few</i> things I'm emphatically not a fan of. So let's get to it.<br /><br /><b>D I S L I K E S:</b><br />• <b>It was tooooo looooong.</b> At 500-pages? Hmm, no. I mean, it did develop the relationships beautifully and complexly. But it definitely dragged when the only things going down where (A) character development, and (B) school. <br />• <b>Too much emphasis on physical beauty.</b> Everyone was drop dead GORGEOUS. I mean, okay. Fine. But everyone???? I like the pretty and the shiny, I DO, but it felt very over-described at times. If I have to hear how handsome Rider is one more time....well. LET ME JUST STAB SOMETHING WITH A SPORK.<br />• <b>I hate how it underlines the fact boys and girls "can't be friends.</b> It seemed to have a huge agenda with this message and I just??? Why???? Everyone was constantly after Rider about "how will his girlfriend feel" if he talks to Mallory. I mean, whut. Obviously this is complicated by the fact Rider/Mallory DO END UP LIKING EACH OTHER (not really a spoiler; because it's super obvious) but it was just insufferable how every time Rider even smiled at Mallory she was thinking "oh but his girlfriend would be mad and has every right to be". No, actually. A relationship shouldn't equal owning another person. If it's that flimsy, I dare say it's not really a relationship.<br />• <b>It was a bit predictable.</b> Maybe I've just read too much?? But I 100% didn't get any surprises at all.<br /><br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL:</b> This was such a good book and it honestly stole a corner of my heart. I am <i>such</i> a magnet to books about tragically abused and suffering characters who need my love. THEY GET ALL MY LOVE. The character development and complexity just shone the whole time. So did the love of enchiladas, bless them. I'm absolutely in love with Rider. It took Mallory a while to figure it out BUT I KNEW FROM THE GET-GO, SO POINTS TO ME. And I love love love the message of <b>believing in yourself and your own worth</b> because it's so important and it's such a relatable message/topic.<br /><br />HELP ME I'M FEELING THINGS AGAIN.<br /><br />If you haven't read this book YOU NEED TO. I can see it in your eyes.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6602612006141341519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Those who want to find their voice.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47555322-poppy?shelf=hyped-books">hyped-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47555322-poppy?shelf=2016-release">2016-release</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1697819908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16183731194533435121"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471542678i/20070331._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Forever was something we all took for granted, but the problem with forever was that it really didn't exist.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471542192i/20070257._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I picked <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26721568.The_Problem_with_Forever' title='The Problem with Forever by Jennifer L. Armentrout' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Problem with Forever</a> with quite an expectations. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4476934.Jennifer_L__Armentrout' title='Jennifer L. Armentrout' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jennifer L. Armentrout</a> was one of my fav authors. I've read almost every book of her. But yet this book was .. just not for me. If you have read the reviews of this book, you must've noticed everyone saying that this book is not our usual fun and quirky JLA read. Well I agree with them, this book really was an exc</span>
  <span id="freeText16183731194533435121" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471542678i/20070331._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Forever was something we all took for granted, but the problem with forever was that it really didn't exist.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471542192i/20070257._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I picked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26721568.The_Problem_with_Forever" title="The Problem with Forever by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">The Problem with Forever</a> with quite an expectations. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4476934.Jennifer_L__Armentrout" title="Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Jennifer L. Armentrout</a> was one of my fav authors. I've read almost every book of her. But yet this book was .. just not for me. If you have read the reviews of this book, you must've noticed everyone saying that this book is not our usual fun and quirky JLA read. Well I agree with them, this book really was an exception but not a good one. At least not for me, though I must say JLA you nailed it with this beautiful cover, unlike anyone of your <b>BEST</b> novels but with a average cover, <i>this was really a exception</i>. Well, I really really don't want to bash this book, though my inner devil is literally glaring at me and saying <i>" Do it, Poppy Do it!!</i><br><br>I must say I really appreciate the struggle that you had to make it more philosophical read, but <i>oh my,</i> Sorry to say I didn't even understand half of the time whatever you were trying to say. There were so many things off with this book. Especially the <b>Main Characters</b> Sorry but i wouldn't have cared if they didn't get a HEA or a HFN or Rider or Mallory died, seriously I was unable to even like them. For me the side characters were MUCH more favourable than the Main Characters. There was no feels. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"...the way he said Mouse was so different from how Paige hurled the nickname. It was soft and deep and infinite."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Why I didn't loved this book??<br><br>✏Like I said I love the side Characters, Jayden, Hector, Paide, Katie and Ainsley- Man everyone!! Every single of side character was my fav one, they literally made me read this book till the end. Even i cried for a side character, if you have read this book you would know what i am talking about.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“As class ended, Hector announced, “I’m hungry.”<br>“ okay,” Rider responded as I said to my notebook into my bag. “ what exactly do you want me to do about it?” <br>Hector grinned as he glanced over at me and winked. “ I want you to take me out and feed me.” Rider snorted.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>✏ The writing, main I wa shocked to see the writing how much JLA's writing has been changed in year since i have last read her books. The more the book was going towards its ending the more i thought; <i>Man where the hell is plot???</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1413104940ra/11465928.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✏ This book was <b>Simply</b> on Mallory and on his... ahh ... speech .. problems because .. of her.. past ..and trauma.. Well <b>Shit</b> Mallory its just a problem. Its not like i don't sympathize with her, i do. What she faced in her childhood was bad but this doesn't describe what you are now. <br><br><blockquote>
  <i>“You're beautiful, too. I mean, you're hot,” I blurted out. “But I always knew you would be.” my eyes widened as I realize what just streamed out of my mouth, and his grin to turn into a smile. “Oh my God, I did not just say... any of that out loud.”<br>“you did” <br>“Ugh.”</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414702262ra/11679932.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✏ The relationship between Mallory and Rider was not upto the point. Like in one half they were dealing with <i>the Ghosts of the foster home duh i mean "mr.henry</i> and then They meet in High School after 4 year and <b>Viola</b> <i>They are in freakin LOVE!!</i>. Not it doesn't end on that, there's more ..<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"Mouse, we can't be together. We've to end this .."<br>"what .. are you talking.. about rider?? why shouldn't we be together."<br>"Mouse.." <br>"Don't call me Mouse, i am not a Mouse anymore, I've changed."<br>"Mous.. Mallory I am leaving you, you deserve better than me."</i>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450457009ra/17429430.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✏ The Main problem was <b>The Name's</b>, <b>Rider Stark</b> <i>Oh, you mean Tony Stark's brother from Civil War as you know their is such a similarity in their names??</i> and then <b>Mallory "Mouse" Dodge</b> <i>Well yeah babe you really shouldn't be dodging in speech but .. in ... life babe!</i><br><br>✏ The metaphor's ..<br><i>"My Blush turned me into the full shade of strawberry."</i><br><i>"His eyes shine like a eclipse."</i><br><i>"The dimple turn in to full smile that makes his eyes shine."</i><br><br>Well, yeah you can understand my feelings.. <br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471464184ra/20057706.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>At the end, you guys MUST be thinking why giving it a <i>
  <b>2 stars, when should give it 1 star,</b>
</i> well because of the story,<i> Not characters, not the drama, not the snob dailouges, not the fake angst, not E.L james metaphor.</i> <b>Just because of story and the message that "Everyone should find their voice, nothing remains Forever."</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Forever wasn't being the one who needed protection. Forever wasn't pain and grief forever wasn't a problem. Forever was my heartbeat and it was the hope tomorrow held. Forever was the glistening silver lining of the dark cloud, no matter how heavy and thick it was. Forever was knowing it moments of weakness didn't equate to an eternity of them. Forever was knowing that I was strong. </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471542678i/20070332._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_1643463252" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1643463252" />
    <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously"><img alt="Rachel Reads Ravenously" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539149211p2/14514998.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1643463252?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel Reads Ravenously" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel Reads Ravenously" href="/user/show/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously">Rachel Reads Ravenously</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=3-stars-aint-the-devil">3-stars-aint-the-devil</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=hardcover">hardcover</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1643463252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7737917827236202601"><b> 3 stars </b><br/><br/>This book............ it had the right idea, but the execution just wasn't quite right. JLA is one of my all time favorite authors, many of you know that because I've been screaming about her books since I discovered them. I enjoyed this book, and I love the concept of it. I just didn't like the execution of it.<br/><br/>This is the story of Mallory, a foster kid who doesn't speak much because of PTSD and conditioning from her previous foster home. Four years later and a nice couple have taken he</span>
  <span id="freeText7737917827236202601" style="display:none"><b> 3 stars </b><br /><br />This book............ it had the right idea, but the execution just wasn't quite right. JLA is one of my all time favorite authors, many of you know that because I've been screaming about her books since I discovered them. I enjoyed this book, and I love the concept of it. I just didn't like the execution of it.<br /><br />This is the story of Mallory, a foster kid who doesn't speak much because of PTSD and conditioning from her previous foster home. Four years later and a nice couple have taken her in and homeschooled her, but now she's going to fulfill her senior year at a public school. On the first day of school she runs into the boy she never thought she would see again, her protector in her old foster home. They are happy to see each other, but their time in that horrible house has left it's mark.<br /><br />I think Mallory's story was an important one to tell, social anxiety stemming from her issues is a tough subject. I feel teens will be able to relate to her as a character and easily empathize with her. It's important for teens to have books they can relate to so they don't feel alone, and this is a perfect one to hand to a teen who has issues with public speaking/ptsd. What I didn't love was this book was looooooooonnnnnnnnnnnnnggggggggg. Like, the message could have been executed in 350 pages instead of 470. Because for me, this book dragged big time. I never had that excitement to pick it back up again once I put it down.<br /><br />I think I am one of the few with this opinion, so please pick it up and try it for yourself. JLA is still one of my favorite authors and I will gladly read anything she publishes in the future, this just wasn't exactly my cup of tea. And oh! This book has a pretty cover. That's another bonus :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="7737917827236202601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1634370799" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1634370799" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1634370799?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog">Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=in-the-minority-on-this-one">in-the-minority-on-this-one</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=skim-tastic">skim-tastic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=unforgettable-male-leads">unforgettable-male-leads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=my-favorite-covers">my-favorite-covers</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1634370799" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12823700931404178181"><br/>I don't know what to say. I really really don't. JLA was my absolute favorite author for two years....<i>two years</i>...and now I feel like she's an acquaintance that used to be a best friend from High School-We pass each other in a store and do that awkward hi/hello/ass-out-hug that plagues us when we <b>realize we no longer have anything in common with our dear old friend</b>. I mean, I knew JLA wasn't for me anymore, I <i>knew</i> that. But I had thought I remembered her writing being more...fluid?? I don't know</span>
  <span id="freeText12823700931404178181" style="display:none"><br>I don't know what to say. I really really don't. JLA was my absolute favorite author for two years....<i>two years</i>...and now I feel like she's an acquaintance that used to be a best friend from High School-We pass each other in a store and do that awkward hi/hello/ass-out-hug that plagues us when we <b>realize we no longer have anything in common with our dear old friend</b>. I mean, I knew JLA wasn't for me anymore, I <i>knew</i> that. But I had thought I remembered her writing being more...fluid?? I don't know. Perhaps it's the fact that I read wonderfully long, fleshed out, beautifully written fantasies now, maybe it's because I'm SO DAMN PICKY with my contemporaries, or perhaps it's just a case of 'it's not you, it's me.' <br><br>For those of you who adore JLA, I'm sure this will be a home run for you. I found that JLA and I stopped seeing eye to eye at the end of the Lux series-her last two books left so much to be desired, in my opinion, because I just had so much love for the first three stories. Hell, her Lux and Covenant series have a bunch of space taken up on my bookshelf because I love them so damn much. I still held out hope for her writing, though, as she began to switch into the contemporary field. Turns out? <b>Her attempt at contemporary stories was the final nail in the coffin</b> for our relationship as I began to see how boring her stories were without the threat of death, mayhem, evil aliens, and crazy deities. If you look back on my older reviews (wait for me, last two lux) you'll see I did rate them highly-this goes back to my 'I don't want to be the only weirdo who is turning on this popular author' days where I didn't have a voice and, frankly, <b>wanted to stay loyal and hold onto the last thread of hope</b> that my favorite author could still do it for me and not turn into someone who failed to make my heart beat faster (aside from my love for the Covenant series and the first three Lux). <br><br>So why in the hell did I read this if I don't like her anymore, you ask? Well...there are <b>a multitude of reasons</b>. I may not think she is as amazing as she used to be after being let down so many times, but I always found her <b>writing addicting as fuck</b>. I ALWAYS loved her story-telling abilities. But here, I found there was a lack of fluidity in the writing (FOR ME, I just didn't connect with her flow) and I had to keep going back to re-read paragraphs just to get the feel of the sentences right. Secondly, <b>this story line seemed epic</b> and unlike anything she has ever done before. But, as it turns out, I was bored from the beginning until about 80% when things finally started to come together and I got to see the deepest parts of our two main characters emerge. I loved seeing Rider's vulnerability and Mallory's voice..it just took forever to get there. Third, <b>she always creates my dream BBFs</b>. *shrugs* I mean, I am who I am lol. And on this front? She delivered. Wonderfully. Lastly? <b>I wanted to love another JLA book</b>...in the deepest part of my heart, I wanted to go back to when JLA was my whole world, I wanted to be proven wrong and find out that I had just become a snooty, pretentious bitch who snubbed her old favorite author. Alas, this didn't happen...in fact, it went the exact opposite way, and that makes me want to cry. <br><br>I know one of my best friends will always love JLA-<i>always</i>. And I sincerely wanted to be that person, again, who fell hard for the author who made me realize I am a peril whore who thrives on that dreadful, heart-shattering cliffhanger (Cough Opal Cough). I mean, guys, <b>she is the author who made me the crazy with want after a crying desperate plea of love perilista</b> I am today-I didn't even know I had this type of masochistic bone in my body (I had read these types of books my whole life but had never realized it was an addiction until JLA) before her, and <b>she shaped my GR name</b>, <b>my reading style</b>, and <b>my whole world</b>. So, yes, I read a book I knew I might not like....but my hope was so much stronger than my common sense and doubt. <br><br>The writing may have not worked for me, but I imagine many of you will find no stilt, no disconnected feeling like I did-<b>it's a personal preference, really</b>. And, as for the main characters, Rider and Mallory, I think that's a personal preference, too. Rider was perfection, no doubt about that, and I felt like skimming all the time until I could get back to him (again, all about the boy, not a good sign). He was sweet, loyal, flawed, and absolutely adorable. <b>When he blushed my heart soared</b> and I became all giddy. When he got all protective of Mallory I fell harder in love. And OMG, the book, guys, that book....*sigh*. <br><br><a href="http://s1301.photobucket.com/user/ChelseaRoberts3/media/LVfxei_zpseuilxuxk.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1463667790ra/19145034.gif" alt=" photo LVfxei_zpseuilxuxk.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But, and this is a small but, I didn't get to bbf status with him....so close, but just, I didn't get <i>enough</i> of him, I guess. He made my heart and stomach do crazy flips, but <b>maybe I was just so bored with the story</b> I didn't give my full attention...and that really sucks.<br><br>As for Mallory....*crickets*. She was fine but....she was the main reason I was bored and her stuttering, while fine when she talked, <b>made her inner monologues grating</b> and hard to read. I might be a bitch, but it's how I felt. And I feel bad because I know that's just how she talks, but I just didn't fall for her as a character.<br><br>So, yeah. I feel bad because there wasn't anything wrong with this story, per se, but I just didn't ever feel 100% immersed. I felt <b>detached and indifferent</b>, most of the time, and only really started loving parts when Rider was in them. <b>Seriously-he was all I looked forward to</b> (I guess I loved him way more than I let on, whoops lol) and was ecstatic when his name or dialogue popped on the page. And, hey, maybe it was the relationship he was involved in that bothered me? Not heavily, but maybe it just bored me that we had to go through that drama, as well. Fuck, guys, I don't know-Here I am, again, saying this horrible phrase: <b>I hated this book....but I loved it, too.</b> Whatever. I don't know. <br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea-peril-please-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452287303i/17673713._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="Twitter" href="https://twitter.com/starcrossedblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660580.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="RSS" href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/starcrossedbookblog/METU" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660581.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="BLOGLOVIN" href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/star-crossed-book-blog-13035961" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a> <a title="Google+" href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/b/116866754719786372049/+Starcrossedbookblog/posts" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

</a><br><br><br>*********<br><br>I'm side eyeing you, JLA<br><br><br>**************<br><br>I know *monkey covering eyes emoji* I added it, anyway, Jen :P</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2779670540" />
    <a title="❥ KAT ❥ Kitty Kats Crazy About Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6245313-kat-kitty-kats-crazy-about-books"><img alt="❥ KAT ❥ Kitty Kats Crazy About Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582051737p2/6245313.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2779670540?book_show_action=true">Apr 08, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="❥ KAT ❥ Kitty Kats Crazy About Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="❥ KAT ❥ Kitty Kats Crazy About Books" href="/user/show/6245313-kat-kitty-kats-crazy-about-books">❥ KAT ❥ Kitty Kats Crazy About Books</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2779670540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6059709930819717640">I'd hit such a book funk, I can't count the amount of books I tried getting into to get me over it, and none held my attention..UNTIL this book..<br/><br/>What an amazing book!! This was so realistic, I could see it all unfolding as I was reading, I connected to the characters whole heartedly, the storyline flowed perfectly, not rushed, easy to get into, but so damn hard to put down, once I’d started that very first chapter I was beyond hooked. <br/>If this throws me into another book funk then I’m going to be</span>
  <span id="freeText6059709930819717640" style="display:none">I'd hit such a book funk, I can't count the amount of books I tried getting into to get me over it, and none held my attention..UNTIL this book..<br /><br />What an amazing book!! This was so realistic, I could see it all unfolding as I was reading, I connected to the characters whole heartedly, the storyline flowed perfectly, not rushed, easy to get into, but so damn hard to put down, once I’d started that very first chapter I was beyond hooked. <br />If this throws me into another book funk then I’m going to be truly f# cked.<br /><br />I loved everything about this book and talk about the feels, this was a fast burn for me, as soon as these two characters reconnected that was it for me I was in my zone going along on this beautiful journey. <br />In my happy place loving these two, they were utter perfection. </span>

<div id="review_1603336695" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1603336695" />
    <a title="TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34338862-thecrazyworldofabooklover"><img alt="TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489089790p2/34338862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1603336695?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover" href="/user/show/34338862-thecrazyworldofabooklover">TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34338862-thecrazyworldofabooklover?shelf=no-just-no">no-just-no</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1603336695" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15966910152617491564">So….<br/><br/><a href='http://s1270.photobucket.com/user/sturano555/media/giphy_zpssps27il6.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467755349ra/19626671.gif' alt=' photo giphy_zpssps27il6.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>This is the author everyone seems to rave about, huh? I have so many book friends who love this author and love her other books. But in all honesty, I don’t see the appeal. I found nothing extraordinary about her writing and nothing made it stand out to me. Maybe it’s me. Or maybe this isn’t her best work; maybe this specific book doesn’t reflect her writing abilities. I think (and am HOPING) it’s the latter.<br/><br/>What didn’t work? What I found incredibly annoying was first and foremost the ac</span>
  <span id="freeText15966910152617491564" style="display:none">So….<br><br><a href="http://s1270.photobucket.com/user/sturano555/media/giphy_zpssps27il6.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1467755349ra/19626671.gif" alt=" photo giphy_zpssps27il6.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This is the author everyone seems to rave about, huh? I have so many book friends who love this author and love her other books. But in all honesty, I don’t see the appeal. I found nothing extraordinary about her writing and nothing made it stand out to me. Maybe it’s me. Or maybe this isn’t her best work; maybe this specific book doesn’t reflect her writing abilities. I think (and am HOPING) it’s the latter.<br><br>What didn’t work? What I found incredibly annoying was first and foremost the actual writing. This author seems to be a HUGE fan of using an excessive amount of commas <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1079467216" rel="nofollow noopener">(and I REALLY HATE THIS TYPE OF WRITING) </a>
</b> and an even bigger fan of ellipses:<br><br><b>
  <i>“The kids in my class will know…that I can’t do it and that I’m getting something..they aren’t. They all…have to stand up there and I don’t? I need to…do it.”<br><br>“I….I didn’t think you’d do that.”<br><br>“Then…you shouldn’t have followed me because….I’m not your problem anymore.”</i>
</b><br><br>After a while, all the “…” in the text was really irritating.<br><br>The book is also unnecessarily LONG. 480 pages of nothing really. And I would have considered the writing issues I had minor details if the actual story was more substantial with a romance that wasn’t <b>
  <i>so freaking stilted.</i>
</b> There was absolutely no quick banter or witty dialogue which is something I look forward to when I read YA. It was like the author was trying really hard to make the reader cry by forcing this awful backstory on the MCs. It didn’t make me cry. Not even once. Not even a little tear. Not even an eye rub. And maybe that's a harsh thing to say, especially considering the tough subjects this book covers. But you know what YA book with a heroine that has a really tragic backstory made me cry my eyes out? That was FILLED with witty banter regardless of the sad undertone of the plot? <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1158291282" rel="nofollow noopener">THIS ONE.</a>
</b><br><br>Another huge issue was Mallory herself. I know a few people who read this said there was WAY too much inner monologue. But an issue the heroine faces is speaking. So I understand the use of it. That isn’t what bothered me. It was that her voice was never authentic. It was all over the place and felt forced. She vacillated between having a really mature thought process to having these immature “teenage” thoughts. And I say “teenage” because it felt like the author wrote her as an adult mimicking an annoying teenager and their slang.<br><br>It all just came off as amateur and this doesn’t seem like a book that was written by a seasoned professional.<br><br>This was a YA book with no soul. I am a firm believer that there are YA books out there that can appeal to all ages <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1158291282" rel="nofollow noopener">(*cough* THIS ONE *cough*)</a>
</b> but this one seemed too juvenile, among the many other issues. I won’t write this author off and plan on reading her other books. But if they are anything like this one, I think I’ll need to just accept her writing isn’t for me.<br><br><a href="https://thecrazyworldofabooklover.wordpress.com/" target="blog" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467902722i/19644381._SX540_.jpg" width="275" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br> <br>Find Me On:<br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/thecrazyworldofabooklover/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ❤ <a href="https://www.facebook.com/profile.php?id=100009277089211" rel="nofollow noopener">FB Page</a> ❤ <a href="https://www.facebook.com/TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover/" rel="nofollow noopener">FB Blog</a> ❤ <a href="https://thecrazyworldofabooklover.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15966910152617491564" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
