    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1623461625" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1623461625" />
    <a title="ambsreads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads"><img alt="ambsreads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508924675p2/30813900.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1623461625?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ambsreads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ambsreads" href="/user/show/30813900-ambsreads">ambsreads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=not-for-me">not-for-me</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30813900-ambsreads?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1623461625" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16229703617815992093"><b>What is 'The Problem with Forever'?</b><br/>The fact it felt like forever for me to finish this book. <br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>“Words were not the enemy or the monster under my bed, but they held such power over me. They were like the ghost of a loved one, forever haunting me."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><i>The Problem With Forever</i> wasn't a bad book at all, but it wasn't good. Well, that's a lie. It was good for the first 40% - I can say that from the fact I had a smile on my face and couldn't put it down once I started reading it last night until my eyes</span>
  <span id="freeText16229703617815992093" style="display:none"><b>What is 'The Problem with Forever'?</b><br />The fact it felt like forever for me to finish this book. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“Words were not the enemy or the monster under my bed, but they held such power over me. They were like the ghost of a loved one, forever haunting me."</i>
</blockquote><br /><br /><i>The Problem With Forever</i> wasn't a bad book at all, but it wasn't good. Well, that's a lie. It was good for the first 40% - I can say that from the fact I had a smile on my face and couldn't put it down once I started reading it last night until my eyes burned. However, when I woke up and continued to read it lost all the charm it had the previous night. It was now boring. It lost every part of the spark that entrapped me in the story and the further I got the more I wanted to DNF it, but I persevered because I hate myself obviously. <br /><br />I usually love every one of JLA's books, they're guilty pleasures and fast reads. However, this one fell completely short. Maybe it was the brief mentioning of things to only be disregarded - e.g. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the fact Mallory had been severely burned. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Or maybe it was the unrealistic nature of people in the book. I never understand when people are afraid of a character in a school like the whole school is afraid of them. I, myself, went to nine different schools and not in one was there a single person everyone was collectively afraid of. Maybe, it's just an American cliche I can't understand. It's just weird. <br /><br />I would like to read a book about the side characters - particularly Ainsley and Hector. They were brilliant characters and honestly made up for the lack of story in the rest of the book. I also wasn't that shocked when <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jayden was shot, I presumed that it was be Mallory who was short and that would lead to Rider breaking up with her for her "safety". <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I was honestly just annoyed by the weakest main characters I have yet to read about. Mallory wasn't able to do anything for herself and Rider honestly just had a death wish. <br /><br /><i>Characters</i><br /><br /><b>Mallory</b> was plain. Thats the best description of her. She was incredibly plain. She carves things out of soap for Gods sake and thats meant to be the quirkest thing about her - keep in mind this particular skill is sparingly mentioned as well. But, Mallory, our sweet never been kisssed and has been homeschooled for four years, is someone I would get sick of quickly. I understand that she has been through things, I'm not being unsympathetic, <i>but</i> she couldn't move on from the past which was infuriating. Things happen and you have to move on from said things is what I have learnt, Mallory, however, liked to dwell on these things and break down. <br /><br />Oh, Mallory's other quirk is she doesn't talk. Well, she does. She's neither mute or shy. She just simply has been conditioned to be quiet and four years away from the house where that happened hasn't changed that. She can barely string four words together without stuttering, and again not to be unsympathetic, it got annoying quickly. I understand it was to provide a deeper picture into what child neglect and abuse can do to someone but it gets a bit tiresome in a 400+ page book, in my opinion at least. <br /><br />She does have a character development, though, this character development happens at 95% of the way through the book, so we don't really get to experience Mallory's <i>change of heart</i>. It was just annoying. She didn't stand up for herself, she was weak, she relied on Rider for the entire part of the book he was in to help her despite the fact he had his own stuff going on. She also never got to know the older Rider, just presuming he had remained the same in the past four years. <br /><br /><b>Rider</b> wasn't as bad as Mallory, but he was still bad. He had a saviour complex around Mallory, he put her on a pedestal and won't ever take her down. It was unrealistic and eye rolling. Sure, every girl and boy deserves someone to love them but there is a point where it reaches creepy and overbearing - at least in my opinion. <br /><br />His character was never developed either. We were expected to think that Rider was the same person he was at like 13 at 18, or whatever their ages were. Everything about his character was unrealistic in the way it was over dramatised. He was painted to be a bad boy, but he was a <i>smart</i> bad boy. Oh wait, no he wasn't actually a bad boy. He was just from the wrong side of town. Which meant none of the teachers cared about him. Which meant that no teachers cared if he went to the wrong lunch. It was just ridiculous how we were expected that teachers and others wouldn't care about him. Some may say that's public schools but I've been to public schools my entire life to know that fact is false. <br /><br />Rider just wasn't the strong and brave character JLA was trying to portray. Of course, at the end, it is shown that he is as messed up as Mallory. Which was pretty damn obvious. <br /><br /><b>Please excuse me while I ram my head into a brick wall because I can't handle this.</b><br /><br /><i>Plot</i><br /><br />The plot was basically between Mallory and Rider. There was no really other deeper, underlying issues. I mean, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jayden dying could have proved to be a major plot point <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, but the plot primary focused on their relationship and how they cared for each other - along with the fact of Paige and their actual problems from the abuse which weren't really acknowledged besides the fact Mallory didn't talk - earning her the nickname Mouse from Rider (which actually came across as condescending each time I read it).<br /><br /><i>Writing</i><br /><br />The writing was classic JLA, and I did enjoy the writing. I just didn't enjoy the self-absorbed characters she created which is what ended with this book falling short for me. I also didn't entirely enjoy the dialogue, cringing at moments as I read it. I mean, I've seen so many people who have enjoyed it and I <b>did</b> enjoy it. Just not to extent I would have though with the beautiful writing in the book.<br /><br /><i>Overall</i><br /><br />Overall, a good book but it personally didn't live up to the hype I was expecting it to. It was slow for the first 70% and then tried to jam way too much in the final 30% that it came across as cliche. This review is slightly all over the place and I've probably contridiced myself several times - but I'm okay with that because thats what this book did.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16229703617815992093" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4124703477934949957"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463135877i/19085183._SX540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><blockquote>
  <pre>
    <b>Emotional. Hopeful. Inspiring.</b>
  </pre>
</blockquote><br/>Growing up in foster care, neglect and abuse are no strangers so Mallory Dodge and Rider Stark. As Six year olds, they were each other’s solaces in a world where they were failed by the adults around them. Years later freedom comes as a result of a particularly harrowing night, but with it, a separation and end to the home they found in one another.<br/><br/>It’s not until four years later, as seniors in high school that they re-enter each other lives. There are s</span>
  <span id="freeText4124703477934949957" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463135877i/19085183._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <pre>
    <b>Emotional. Hopeful. Inspiring.</b>
  </pre>
</blockquote><br>Growing up in foster care, neglect and abuse are no strangers so Mallory Dodge and Rider Stark. As Six year olds, they were each other’s solaces in a world where they were failed by the adults around them. Years later freedom comes as a result of a particularly harrowing night, but with it, a separation and end to the home they found in one another.<br><br>It’s not until four years later, as seniors in high school that they re-enter each other lives. There are some powerful moments shared and what takes place is the a story of love, loss and discovery. I was moved by JLA’s descriptions, her emotive style of writing and the overwhelming admiration I have for Mallory and Rider. <br><br>I always feel as though I’m in safe hands when it comes too JLA and YA. The reticence I usually feel about the sub genre dissipated within the first few pages of The Problem with Forever. There is such depth in both the storyline and characters, the only problem I had was putting it down.<br><br><a href="http://relentlessromance.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1460975058i/18808976._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1645927277" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13497832384194756583">5 Stars!!<br/><br/>Excellent writing, This is my first read from this Author for this genre. I not only fell in love with the cover and the blurb but the storyline is well written. With so many Young Adult coming of age books out I have to say this one is my top five. So many ways I thought the author was going to take us and boom she does something I didn't expect. The heartbreaking scene left me is tears. I know that our children services protection is so overwhelmed that when we read about the lives th</span>
  <span id="freeText13497832384194756583" style="display:none">5 Stars!!<br /><br />Excellent writing, This is my first read from this Author for this genre. I not only fell in love with the cover and the blurb but the storyline is well written. With so many Young Adult coming of age books out I have to say this one is my top five. So many ways I thought the author was going to take us and boom she does something I didn't expect. The heartbreaking scene left me is tears. I know that our children services protection is so overwhelmed that when we read about the lives these children sometimes endure is heartwrenching. <br />This is a story about a boy and a girl under ten who survived being in the foster care system. The abuse these two individuals is heartbreaking. This is their story 5 years later after a night of terror and seperation. They reunite and find each other in different places and how one gets the helped needed and the other not. I recommend this read for all to understand when a human life is broken there is help. In order to get help that person needs to be willing to want it.</span>

<div id="review_1648359872" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1648359872" />
    <a title="~♡AB♡~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12180287-ab"><img alt="~♡AB♡~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555104554p2/12180287.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1648359872?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~♡AB♡~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~♡AB♡~" href="/user/show/12180287-ab">~♡AB♡~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12180287-ab?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12180287-ab?shelf=3-and-a-half-stars-it-was-good">3-and-a-half-stars-it-was-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12180287-ab?shelf=super-angsty">super-angsty</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12180287-ab?shelf=second-chance-love">second-chance-love</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1648359872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12725162385882572773">★★★ <b>3.5 Stars</b> ★★★<br/><br/>The Problem with Forever is a story that touches on the lives of two high school seniors who are both products of the foster care system, and who share a bond that is deep and unbreakable.<br/><br/>Mallory Dodge is one of the lucky ones, and after a horrific childhood where the only person who showed her any love was her foster brother, she is now living with caring and understanding adoptive parents. It's been four years since she was ripped away from the boy who used to protect her from</span>
  <span id="freeText12725162385882572773" style="display:none">★★★ <b>3.5 Stars</b> ★★★<br><br>The Problem with Forever is a story that touches on the lives of two high school seniors who are both products of the foster care system, and who share a bond that is deep and unbreakable.<br><br>Mallory Dodge is one of the lucky ones, and after a horrific childhood where the only person who showed her any love was her foster brother, she is now living with caring and understanding adoptive parents. It's been four years since she was ripped away from the boy who used to protect her from the monsters that were supposed to care for her, and not a day has gone by when she didn't think about what became of him.<br><br>Choosing to transition from homeschooling to completing her senior year at the High School, she is knocked for six when she discovers that Rider Stark is also a student there.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"We’d been separated. But we had never really been apart."</b>
</blockquote><br>I loved the hero, Rider - he was a fiercely loyal and protective young man, who was confident and outgoing on the outside, but with deep insecurities and an extreme amount of guilt on the inside. <br><br>Mallory was harder to connect to, she was extremely shy and introverted which sometimes came across as bland, but I couldn't help but root for her to come out of her shell and start living. I do feel however that younger readers will be more able to relate to her and her worries.<br><br>The book was quite long and Mallory's inner monologue was quite testing at times, but the tender moments between Mallory and Rider made up for that. I also loved the side characters, Rider's foster brothers and even Paige, who was Rider's girlfriend at the start of the book.<br><br>Overall, it was a sweet read that tackled teen issues in a way that left you with hope and admiration for the two main characters.<br><br><b>The Problem with Forever is a young adult romance, told in Mallory's POV.</b><br><br><i>ARC gratefully received from Harlequin (UK) Limited in exchange for an honest review</i><br><br> 
  <a href="https://www.facebook.com/ilovebooklove" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455711019i/18139362.png" alt="facebook" width="32" height="32" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>
  <a href="https://twitter.com/ilovebooklove" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2217584096?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780373212248" href="/book/show/30227861-the-problem-with-forever">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=emotionally-intense">emotionally-intense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=physically-owned-books">physically-owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=five-stars">five-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=unexpectedly-good">unexpectedly-good</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=auto-buy-authors">auto-buy-authors</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2217584096" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3421262951851002890"><pre>
  <b> <i> “Forever wasn’t pain and grief. <br/>Forever wasn’t a problem. <br/>Forever was my heartbeat and it was the hope tomorrow <br/>held. <br/>Forever was the glistening silver lining of every <br/>dark cloud, no matter how heavy and thick it was. <br/>Forever was knowing weakness didn’t equate <br/>to an eternity of them” </i></b>
</pre><br/><br/>Life taught me that sometimes you have to protect your heart from beautiful things because when they break or shatter or when I finally look at them up close and find an irreparable damage, it breaks my heart.</span>
  <span id="freeText3421262951851002890" style="display:none"><pre>
  <b> <i> “Forever wasn’t pain and grief. <br>Forever wasn’t a problem. <br>Forever was my heartbeat and it was the hope tomorrow <br>held. <br>Forever was the glistening silver lining of every <br>dark cloud, no matter how heavy and thick it was. <br>Forever was knowing weakness didn’t equate <br>to an eternity of them” </i></b>
</pre><br><br>Life taught me that sometimes you have to protect your heart from beautiful things because when they break or shatter or when I finally look at them up close and find an irreparable damage, it breaks my heart. This is how I felt about reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26721568.The_Problem_with_Forever" title="The Problem with Forever by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">The Problem with Forever</a>. I was very cautious that even though I wanted to embrace the characters close to my heart, be involved with their story and feel their emotions, my instincts told me not to get too attached because for some reason, I knew it was going to be tragic. <br><br>I was wrong though.<br><br>And honestly, even if I tried to control my emotions and even if the book did end tragically (which it didn’t, just partly because <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[*Jayden! Cries!* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>), I would have still fallen in love with the story and the characters because how could I not? I wanted to protect little <b>Mallory</b> and <b>Rider</b> from everything they went through. <br><br>Reading their story made me want to change my career to being a social worker if only it were possible. My heart ached for the only kind of life they knew as children so thank goodness for second chances, for kind strangers who foster and adopt children and love them like their own.<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26721568.The_Problem_with_Forever" title="The Problem with Forever by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">The Problem with Forever</a> has been at the top of my wish list since it was published. For some reason, I felt very drawn to that cover and to that title so I did everything I could to find my copy and I’m very glad it didn’t disappoint. <br><br>But as significant as the story is, know that this book is basically a romance novel between a girl and a boy whose past has forever marked them in both good ways and bad so it’s a bit angsty, cheesy, sometimes corny but really adorable and inspiring. Both Mallory and Rider but Mallory especially are admirable characters and their story is one that I would cherish and probably read over and over, possibly forever. ;)<br><br>Here’s the perfect song for the book. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513574893i/24701081._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="3421262951851002890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1385301774" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1385301774" />
    <a title="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog"><img alt="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1576986930p2/28353412.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1385301774?book_show_action=true">Sep 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥" href="/user/show/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog">Jen ♥Star-Crossed Book Blog♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=good-boys-i-love">good-boys-i-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=sigh-bbf">sigh-bbf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=insta-not-used">insta-not-used</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=dont-cry">dont-cry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=hot-hot-hot">hot-hot-hot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=romance-friends-to-lovers">romance-friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/28353412-jen-star-crossed-book-blog?shelf=arcs">arcs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1385301774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14269779042369685813"><b>The Problem With Forever was an emotionally haunting and beautiful story.</b> Reading the prologue alone, I knew that I was stepping into a book that would forever be ingrained in my heart. Not only because this was a first for me, since <b>I cried from the prologue.</b> To think about children suffering through that type of physical and emotional abuse hurts me to the core. But that wasn't the only reason why this story will stay with me forever. <b>Mallory and Rider enraptured me with their feelings.</b> I beca</span>
  <span id="freeText14269779042369685813" style="display:none"><b>The Problem With Forever was an emotionally haunting and beautiful story.</b> Reading the prologue alone, I knew that I was stepping into a book that would forever be ingrained in my heart. Not only because this was a first for me, since <b>I cried from the prologue.</b> To think about children suffering through that type of physical and emotional abuse hurts me to the core. But that wasn't the only reason why this story will stay with me forever. <b>Mallory and Rider enraptured me with their feelings.</b> I became obsessed with The Problem With Forever as we transitioned to High School in the first chapter, and that obsession never once wavered.<br><blockquote>
  <b>Words were not the enemy or the monster under my bed, but they held such power over me. They were like the ghost of a loved one, forever haunting me.</b>
</blockquote><br>Mallory Dodge was unlike any other character I have met. She was timid, she was overwhelmed by noise, and she had been trained not to make a sound. While she was a foster child, she spent her youth learning that sounds and noises brought attention to herself. And with attention came physical and emotional abuse. And <b>while I have never once felt nervous, overwhelmed or panicky about the thought of speaking to others, Mallory made me feel terrified right along with her. </b> My palms were sweaty and my stomach was tossing and turning with nervousness. Mallory made me feel every single thing she did! Yet as the story unfolded, <b>we got to see Mallory push herself out of her comfort zone again and again. </b> I loved how we got to watch Mallory grow and find strength within herself. She was an amazing woman!<br><blockquote>
  <b>“Do you recognize me?” His voice was still barely above a whisper.<br>His eyes continued to hold mine, and I spoke what turned out to be the easiest word I’d ever said in my life.<br>“Yes.”</b>
</blockquote><br>But what Mallory could never had predicted was running into Rider Stark on her first day going back to public school. Rider was a foster child who had grown up in the same house as Mallory. They had been together from the age of 3, until they were separated at 13. Although four years had passed since they last saw each other, it's hard to forget that they were each others world. Especially for Mallory. <b>Not only was Rider her best friend, but he was her protector too. He took beatings that </b><b>
  <i>she</i>
</b><b> was meant to take. He sacrificed himself to protect Mallory and keep her safe at all costs.</b> Until they were ripped apart.<br><blockquote>
  <b>My heart exploded as those strong arms pulled me against his chest. There was a moment where I froze, and then my arms swept around his neck. I held on, squeezing my eyes shut as I inhaled the clean scent and the lingering trace of aftershave. This was </b>
  <b>
    <i>him</i>
  </b>
  <b>. His hugs were different now, stronger and tighter. He lifted me clear off my feet, one arm around my waist, the other hand buried deep in my hair, and my breasts were mushed against his surprisingly hard chest.<br>Whoa.</b>
</blockquote><br><b>Rider was breathtaking. </b> Not only because of what he did in the past for Mallory, but those actions continued through to present day. <b>Rider stepped back into Mallory's life and became her protector all over again.</b> He would do the sweetest things like ditch a class so that way Mallory would have someone to sit and eat lunch with. Just wait till you see everything he did for Mallory, he was such a good guy! But some aspects of their relationship did change over time. Sexual tension was strumming between them and it was sigh and toe curling worthy. Rider literally gave me chills with his words and mannerisms towards Mallory. So yeah, I became a little obsessed with him lol. <b>Rider was charming, sexy, sweet, loyal, dedicated and the intensity of how much he still cared for Mallory lifted off of the pages. It was impossible not to fall for him.</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>I pulled myself out of the memory, but there were so many of him coming to my rescue for some reason or another until he couldn’t, until the promise of forever had been shattered, and everything… everything had fallen apart.</b>
</blockquote><br>I loved how it felt like I knew Mallory and Rider inside out, especially with the<b> flashbacks to their younger years. Whether it was just a short moment or a longer memory, we got to watch their friendship unfold. And we also got to truly understand all of the horrors that they lived with. </b> It was easy to grasp that they only had each other to rely on. And how their past helped form them into the person that they would become.<br><blockquote>
  <b>His lashes lowered and the lopsided grin appeared. “I always knew you’d be beautiful one day.”<br>My breath hitched as I sat straighter. What was left of the pizza , just the crust, was totally forgotten . My ears had to be smoking crack or something.<br>A flush swept across his cheeks as one side of his lips kicked up. “I just never thought I’d get to see how beautiful you’d become.”</b>
</blockquote><br>The Problem With Forever also contained moments with Mallory's best friend who I absolutely adored! It was refreshing to see a strong female friendship, and I can't wait for Ainsley's book! And I was happy to see that Mallory's adoptive parents played an active role in some very important moments in Mallory's life. But <b>when I closed that last page, I was struck by how extremely grateful I am for my life.</b> I was reminded of all of the positives that constantly surround me, no matter how little or big they are. And I'm so glad that message, whether intentional or not, sunk it's claws into me. So of course <b>I loved every single moment in The Problem With Forever, and I hope you will too.</b><br><br><i>*ARC kindly provided by Harlequin TEEN via Inkslinger PR in exchange for an honest review*</i><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i> <br><a title="Star-Crossed Book Blog" href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452287496i/17673736._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b> </b>
</u><br><a title="Facebook" href="https://www.facebook.com/starcrossedbookblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="Twitter" href="https://twitter.com/starcrossedblog" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660580.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <a title="RSS" href="http://feeds.feedburner.com/starcrossedbookblog/METU" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660581.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2097913899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6351183918344984909">This is a story that's going to stick with me for a long time. It was such a beautiful contemporary! My heart was completely shattered from all the feels, but it was totally worth it.<br/><br/>Mallory was a wonderful protagonist. Rider was incredible. Ainsley was the best and I wish all YA novels had a character like her. It was brilliantly cute and adorable, yet also realistic and dealt with some serious issues. It was upfront and honest, but a beautiful read. I would highly recommend.</span>

<div id="review_1645293830" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1645293830" />
    <a title="Jasmine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine"><img alt="Jasmine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582366251p2/21803154.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1645293830?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine" href="/user/show/21803154-jasmine">Jasmine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who likes to have a light yet meaningful read</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=realism">realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=just-fine">just-fine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=never-read-it-again">never-read-it-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=skimming-through">skimming-through</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=happy-ending">happy-ending</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=ebooks-ibooks">ebooks-ibooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21803154-jasmine?shelf=abusive-domestic-violence">abusive-domestic-violence</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1645293830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11298462963155599681"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Life was like doing this speech. It wasn't necessarily about the end result, but more about trying.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>This book is so not the typical Jennifer L. Armentrout style. <b><i>The Problem with Forever</i> is a story about lessons of life, love, family, and reflection on our society nowadays.</b> I know this may sound very serious and stone-cold cruel, but that's the way it is. We all need to accept and endure it. <br/><br/>The story mainly focuses on <b>Mallory (Mouse), a quiet girl who is deemed as a mute in school be</b></span>
  <span id="freeText11298462963155599681" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Life was like doing this speech. It wasn't necessarily about the end result, but more about trying.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This book is so not the typical Jennifer L. Armentrout style. <b><i>The Problem with Forever</i> is a story about lessons of life, love, family, and reflection on our society nowadays.</b> I know this may sound very serious and stone-cold cruel, but that's the way it is. We all need to accept and endure it. <br><br>The story mainly focuses on <b>Mallory (Mouse), a quiet girl who is deemed as a mute in school because of her post-traumatic childhood experience, and Rider, a seemingly open-minded, extroverted guy who actually bears some unspeakable scars on his stained soul.</b> They are both orphans and adopted by the same family when they're little but under the mask of kindness, they fall victim to domestic violence. Rider protects Mallory at all costs and she learns not to make a noise whenever her adopted father gets mad after drinking. <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>Rider had said nothing lasted forever, but some things, some scars, ran too deep to ever fade away.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Therefore, she gets used to stay quiet no matter where she is, no matter what she does. It becomes a part of her life and her voice seems like a stranger to her. <b>She loses her confidence, and she can't seem to enjoy the rest of life because the shadow dwelling in her heart is too dark to get away.</b> Thus, when she meets Rider by chance in school, he's the only key to her closed mind. And teaches her how to live her life. <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"It's just that I think sometimes you miss what's going on around you, because you're so worried about what others are thinking about you and your choices."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Rider has his own problem as well. He seems like a happy-go-lucky at first, but he's one of the troublemakers (or at least he used to be). <b>There's no denying that there are more or less some problematic teenagers/youngsters around the world; they become drug dealers, trade their lives for contraband, and bargain with demons or the Death.</b> These people never stop existing and I think it's time we faced the reality. <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>In that moment, I knew I couldn't hold what he used to do against him. Rider...Jayden...so many other people were a product of their environment. Some got out. Others didn't.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>I hate to say this, but <b>the biggest disappointment is that the story is too predictable.</b> The plot is simple and the inspiration behind all these is easy to grasp, however, this book doesn't make me wow. It doesn't surprise me at all. For example, it's not that hard to guess from the minute Mallory and Rider meet, their relationship is going to develop into something more than friends. I mean, she's apparently drawn to him and he finds her grow maturely and attractive. Also, both of them are adolescents so overloaded hormones drive them toward each other like two inseparable magnets. <blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>"Understand what?" I whispered. Rider's gaze held mine again. "She understands that if I have to pick between you two, it's not going to be her."</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>Yikes, cliche alert! This book reminds me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22522202.Until_Friday_Night__The_Field_Party___1_" title="Until Friday Night (The Field Party, #1) by Abbi Glines" rel="nofollow noopener">Until Friday Night</a>, which is one of the top disappointing books of mine this year, because of the similar plots. (Quiet girl with broken guy, blah blah blah...)<br><br>The only thing interests me is probably the idea of "forever" in the story. I keep looking for signs of forever since the title of the book mentions it but not until the very end of the entire book did I finally get the metaphor. Real life isn't a fantasy, and sometimes even fantasies aren't necessarily fantasies, either. Just like <i>forever</i>, what is forever? Have you thought about the meaning of forever before? It's not just a time period, nor is it some dimensional measurement. This book lets us know that there are actually two kinds of forever. And what lies in between. <blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>The good kind. The bad kind. I'd learned early on that the good kind of forever was, well, it was a lie. That kind of forever literally and figuratively ended in flames, because no matter how tightly you tried to hold on, that kind of forever slipped between the fingers. <br>The bad kind of forever lingered like a shadow or ghost. No matter what. It stayed, always in the background.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>All in all, I may not enjoy the book as much as I do for JLA's other works, I'll still recommend this to those who like to read something light and yet with in-depth meanings between the lines. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467187370i/19561354._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="11298462963155599681" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1628220232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1628220232" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48100672-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602456592p2/48100672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1628220232?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/48100672-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48100672-amanda?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1628220232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14613625518766634631"><b>Thank you to Harlequin (UK) Limited & Jennifer L. Armentrout for my copy of the ARC in exchange for an honest review.</b><br/><br/>Anyone who knows me knows I absolutely adore Jennifer L. Armentrout, she is one of my favourite authors so much so that I still haven't read the last book in The Lux Series because I'm not ready to let go of Katy & Daemon, but for some reason I just couldn't click with this book it kills me to say it!<br/><br/>After an unfortunate upbringing through the care system, Mallory has spent years </span>
  <span id="freeText14613625518766634631" style="display:none"><b>Thank you to Harlequin (UK) Limited &amp; Jennifer L. Armentrout for my copy of the ARC in exchange for an honest review.</b><br /><br />Anyone who knows me knows I absolutely adore Jennifer L. Armentrout, she is one of my favourite authors so much so that I still haven't read the last book in The Lux Series because I'm not ready to let go of Katy &amp; Daemon, but for some reason I just couldn't click with this book it kills me to say it!<br /><br />After an unfortunate upbringing through the care system, Mallory has spent years in therapy trying to get over it. So when she finally gets ready to get herself back to mainstream school after years of homeschooling she never imagines she will run into Rider the only person who loved, protected and understood her growing up. Not only is this a shock to Mallory it also takes Rider by surprise, after and accident that caused both them to be separated he never thought he would get to see his precious mouse again. After four years down the line and both of them in better places is life really what it seems? <br /><br />To be honest, most of the first half of the book didn't captivate me I was getting bored willing for it to give me something that would catch me but it never happened, I wanted it to so bad believe me but sadly it was not meant to be. Getting into the second half of the book I started to like our characters but I never really felt much of a connection like I would have hoped. <br /><br />After reading so much of Mallory not speaking I wanted to scream please for the love of god say something anything and it did start to grate on me, I do like her and the way you see her grow and flourish into a women is lovely, but for me, it was the other characters who made it. Rider had my heart out on a line from the beginning I just wanted to wrap him up in my arms and never let him go, it actually breaks my heart to think that there are stories like this happening and it made admire him even more and it made me take a complete dislike to Carl.<br /><br />So I had a few favourites, obviously Rider but I loved Mallory's best friend Ainsley she was always so upbeat and supportive no matter what was going on and I love that there was Hector who's dirty mouth had me giggling about him and Ainsley it was hilarious. Then there was Jayden, he holds a special place in my heart, I love outgoing cheeky chaps who are witty and full of self-confidence they always make me laugh and are my favourite characters in any Armentrout's books.<br /><br />The book really touches on some of the horrible things kids can go through in the system that actually cuts deep if you really think about it and I think Jennifer touched on them pretty well. I did enjoy the end of the book and I was rooting for everyone as the story was coming to a close and I still have loads of questions, will Mal go to prom?! PLEASE, I HAVE TO KNOW!<br /><br />So one last thing that always gets me with Jennifer's books, I love how she is devoted to safe sex but still makes you feel completely and utterly legless swooning over each private moment... safe sex is important kids remember this!<br /><br /><u>Check out my blog <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.amandaminnockx.tumblr.com">www.amandaminnockx.tumblr.com</a> thanks :)</u><br /><br /><i>
  <b>"I know you deserve better, but I want to be better. I want to be that for you." His voice dropped low as he stopped in front of me. "That's why I'm going to ask what I'm about to."<br />The fluttering was deep in my chest and in my stomach. I felt breathless as I stared into his eyes. "Ask me what?"<br />A muscle flickered along his jaw as his chest rose sharply. "Can I kiss you?"</b>
</i></span>

<div id="review_1637452501" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1637452501" />
    <a title="TJ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3982894-tj"><img alt="TJ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591666758p2/3982894.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1637452501?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TJ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TJ" href="/user/show/3982894-tj">TJ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3982894-tj?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3982894-tj?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1637452501" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4505268069180907771"><b>THE REVIEW</b><br/><br/><b>Why this book?</b><br/><br/>Jen (in her Unicorn Bubble)’s review made me want to read it<br/><br/><b>What I thought</b><br/><br/>This book will always be in my heart. Mallory and Rider were two characters who were emotionally abused who lost eachother and found one another years later. I listened to the audiobook so listening to Mallory try to talk was hard for me, it was heartbreaking. No girl should be conditioned not to make noise. I loved how Rider was always there for her when they were younger and when the see eachother</span>
  <span id="freeText4505268069180907771" style="display:none"><b>THE REVIEW</b><br /><br /><b>Why this book?</b><br /><br />Jen (in her Unicorn Bubble)’s review made me want to read it<br /><br /><b>What I thought</b><br /><br />This book will always be in my heart. Mallory and Rider were two characters who were emotionally abused who lost eachother and found one another years later. I listened to the audiobook so listening to Mallory try to talk was hard for me, it was heartbreaking. No girl should be conditioned not to make noise. I loved how Rider was always there for her when they were younger and when the see eachother again years later. Rider life was also heartbreaking he didn’t feel like he deserved anything, like he wasn’t good enough. They needed eachother and I’m glad they found one another again. Mallory grew so much through the book and I was rooting for her all the way. I got to say Rider was my favorite character he was absolutely swoonworthly. Overall a must read!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4505268069180907771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1635101520" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1635101520" />
    <a title="Vilma Iris" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15777655-vilma-iris"><img alt="Vilma Iris" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1501855386p2/15777655.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1635101520?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vilma Iris" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vilma Iris" href="/user/show/15777655-vilma-iris">Vilma Iris</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1635101520" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3429091273222407342">Jennifer L. Armentrout tackles big issues with a moving story about friendship, love, courage and overcoming the kind of past that scars beneath the surface. With The Problem With Forever, she’s taken her singular style of storytelling to places she’s not yet explored while still delivering a sizzling romance with off-the-charts chemistry. Tender moments accentuate the tragic underpinning from which the protagonists’ lives have been built from—a past riddled with abuse, days paralyzed by fear, a</span>
  <span id="freeText3429091273222407342" style="display:none">Jennifer L. Armentrout tackles big issues with a moving story about friendship, love, courage and overcoming the kind of past that scars beneath the surface. With The Problem With Forever, she’s taken her singular style of storytelling to places she’s not yet explored while still delivering a sizzling romance with off-the-charts chemistry. Tender moments accentuate the tragic underpinning from which the protagonists’ lives have been built from—a past riddled with abuse, days paralyzed by fear, and a stubborn sense of unworthiness that has followed two foster kids over the years.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“He was only six months older than her six years, but he always seemed so much bigger, older than her, because in her eyes, he took up her entire world.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Mallory Dodge and Rider Stark grew up in a foster home where fear, alcohol, drug use and violence were everyday things they saw and experienced. They held on to each other to survive their childhood, in particular, Rider shielded Mallory as best he could. He took the blows, literally and figuratively, so that she would be okay. Mallory learned to keep quiet—sounds had awful repercussions.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“I promised I’d keep you safe forever. Just don’t make a sound.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>One day, everything went wrong and the situation escalated, separating Mallory and Rider when they were both removed from the home.<br><br>Years pass without contact. Mallory is adopted by two kind, wealthy physicians who help her heal, but she’s got a long way to go. After years of home schooling, she pushes herself to attend public high school in efforts to take the next, brave step in shedding the shackles of her past.<br><br>She never expected to see the boy who’d saved her time and again—Rider Stark.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“…the promise of forever had been shattered, and everything… everything had fallen apart.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>After four years apart, their emotional ties easily tangle back together, but it becomes clear their lives have followed divergent paths. Rider didn’t fall into the kind of life that Mallory found, and instead has toed a dangerous line.<br><br>While their connection pushes them together, insecurities, fears and new dynamics makes things more complicated. Mallory fears she can’t overcome her issues, she realizes she can’t depend on Rider to always make things right.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“You can’t … step in every time you think something happens. You can’t always… protect me.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>But as Rider’s life begins to spin out of control, Mallory realizes the seemingly confident Rider bears scars of his own which can threaten everything between them.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“I know you deserve better, but I want to be better. I want to be that for you.”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>I loved this book! I loved the multiracial characters, the exploration of meaningful issues, the blazing, unstoppable chemistry between Mallory and Rider, and the many moving moments in their story. Jennifer’s irresistible wit is still woven here and there, as well as a healthy dose of tension to offer a softening counterpoint to the story’s more serious themes. Well balanced, emotive and painfully real, The Problem With Forever is a gripping novel that shouldn’t be missed.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“We have a second chance. And who gets second chances?”</blockquote>
</b><br><br>✦ ✦ ✦ ✦<br><br><b> Follow Vilma's Book Blog: </b> <a href="http://vilmasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Website</a> | <a href="www.facebook.com/vilmasbookblog" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/vilmasbookblog" rel="nofollow noopener"> Twitter </a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/_vilmagonzalez/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1454604042i/17990720._SX540_.jpg" width="425.50" height="157.5" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="3429091273222407342" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1650419076" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1650419076" />
    <a title="Megan✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25781525-megan-steamy-reads-blog"><img alt="Megan✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1514899021p2/25781525.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1650419076?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦" href="/user/show/25781525-megan-steamy-reads-blog">Megan✦❋Steamy Reads Blog❋✦</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25781525-megan-steamy-reads-blog?shelf=emotional">emotional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25781525-megan-steamy-reads-blog?shelf=ya-romance">ya-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25781525-megan-steamy-reads-blog?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25781525-megan-steamy-reads-blog?shelf=high_school_college_love">high_school_college_love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25781525-megan-steamy-reads-blog?shelf=messed-up">messed-up</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1650419076" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17880806739369432832"><b>
  <i>****4 Stars****</i>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465740027i/19395512.jpg' width='200' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Some secrets go too deep for words.”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Before I had even started this book I knew it would be an unforgettable story. I had a preconceived idea that this was going to be heartbreaking, but it was a story of perseverance through adversity and the ability to rise up and succeed with the challenges that life throws at you. Jennifer L Armentrout seriously bought her A game with a story that deals with some tough emotional issues.<br/><br/>Mallory (Mouse) and Rider grew up together in a f</span>
  <span id="freeText17880806739369432832" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>****4 Stars****</i>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465740027i/19395512.jpg" width="200" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>
  <i>“Some secrets go too deep for words.”</i>
</b><br><br>Before I had even started this book I knew it would be an unforgettable story. I had a preconceived idea that this was going to be heartbreaking, but it was a story of perseverance through adversity and the ability to rise up and succeed with the challenges that life throws at you. Jennifer L Armentrout seriously bought her A game with a story that deals with some tough emotional issues.<br><br>Mallory (Mouse) and Rider grew up together in a foster home and were no strangers to abuse and neglect. All they had was each other. Rider became Mallory’s protector and therefore defended her whenever she was in danger to the point of putting himself in harms-way. He endured a lot of abuse in order to prevent Mallory from being the target. They shared a really special connection. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1465740428i/19395567.jpg" width="250" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>
  <i>“We've been separated. But we had never really been apart.”</i>
</b><br><br>All the suffering and abuse finally came to a horrific climax where ultimately Mallory and Rider were separated. Mallory was in hospital for a period of time and was then adopted by two doctors Carlos and Rosa, who soon became the kind of parents Mallory longed for. Rider was moved to yet another group home until he was fostered again.<br><br>After years of home-schooling, Mallory decides to spend her senior year at a public high school. On her first day she notices a student enter the class room, who then approaches and sits in the spare chair next to her. It’s none other than Rider. They haven’t seen each other in four years and this gave them a second chance to reconnect. <br><br><b>
  <i>“I just never thought I'd get to see how beautiful you'd become”</i>
</b><br><br>Their first meeting at school, even though expected, was still enthralling. I’m so impressed Jennifer L Armentrout avoided insta-love. I expected it to be honest, but was so thrilled it didn’t turn out like that and I loved the anticipation that it teased. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1465741081ra/19395642.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>
  <i>“Forever was something we all took for granted, but the problem with forever was that it really didn't exist.”</i>
</b><br><br>I was really pleased with this story and it was a solid 4 stars. I would recommend this to anyone who loves YA romances, with a background story of abuse, but it is by no means graphic. It is a really sweet story which deals with abuse and their lasting long term effects.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17880806739369432832" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uVO0xfgBskZ6geO0mfyF2Zk3CFs9o8YFZltKh4HZNZumVQCsHdpNyFEF0X0F9uRUSc1Rmg49cOgc1AMrxvpvQA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3KXaKNEezEtPRsecMJebaa79qJ2bZNoXyxkBORhyYHzDo25BNMUzxWTC9VWsnfrkfgfxXKj6bPqxlkiVX1E6pw==')})
  }

I also do NOT check my Goodreads email.<br /><br />To email me, please use the below addy. <br />jenniferlarmentrout@live.com<br /><br /># 1 New York Times and # 1 International Bestselling author Jennifer lives in Charles Town, West Virginia. All the rumors you’ve heard about her state aren’t true. When she’s not hard at work writing. she spends her time reading, watching really bad zombie movies, pretending to write, hanging out with her husband and her Jack Russell Loki. In early 2015, Jennifer was diagnosed with retinitis pigmentosa, a group of rare genetic disorders that involve a breakdown and death of cells in the retina, eventually resulting in loss of vision, among other complications. Due to this diagnosis, educating people on the varying degrees of blindness has become of passion of hers, right alongside writing, which she plans to do as long as she can. <br /><br />Her dreams of becoming an author started in algebra class, where she spent most of her time writing short stories….which explains her dismal grades in math. Jennifer writes young adult paranormal, science fiction, fantasy, and contemporary romance. She is published with Tor, HarperCollins Avon and William Morrow, Entangled Teen and Brazen, Disney/Hyperion and Harlequin Teen. Her Wicked Series has been optioned by PassionFlix. Jennifer has won numerous awards, including the 2013 Reviewers Choice Award for Wait for You, the 2015 Editor’s Pick for Fall With Me, and the 2014/2015 Moerser-Jugendbuch- Jury award for Obsidian. Her young adult romantic suspense novel DON’T LOOK BACK was a 2014 nominated Best in Young Adult Fiction by YALSA. Her adult romantic suspense novel TILL DEATH was a Amazon Editor’s Pick and iBook Book of the Month. Her young adult contemporary THE PROBLEM WITH FOREVER is a 2017 RITA Award Winner in Young Adult Fiction. She also writes Adult and New Adult contemporary and paranormal romance under the name J. Lynn. She is published by Entangled Brazen and HarperCollins.<br /><br />She is the owner of ApollyCon and The Origin Event, the successful annual events that features over hundred bestselling authors in Young Adult, New Adult, and Adult Fiction, panels, parties, and more.</span>
